Given a causal graph G, two nodes V1 and V2 are d-separated by a set of nodes S if and only if:

1. There is no directed path from V1 to V2 that goes through a node in S.
2. There is no directed path from V2 to V1 that goes through a node in S.

In your case, we are asked if V12 and V49 are d-separated given V9. Since V12 and V49 are not nodes in your original graph, I assume you meant to ask about V1 and V9 (or maybe V4 and V9, but we'll get to that later).

* There is a directed path from V4 to V9.

To summarize:

* V1 and V9 are d-separated.
* V4 and V9 are not d-separated.

* V3 -> V6 (direct causal effect)
* V6 -> V7 (direct causal effect)

* V8 -> V9 (direct causal effect)
